href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-vaccine-protection-covid-hospitalization-compared-pfizer-cdc-study-2021-9\">Another CDC report</a> released earlier in September suggested that Moderna's two-dose vaccine reduced the risk of hospitalization by 93%. For Pfizer, that figure was 88%, and for Johnson &#38; Johnson it was 71%.</p><p>Dr. Robert Atmar, who's&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/booster-vaccine-trial-mix-and-match-shots-pfizer-moderna-jandj-2021-6\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"eb3c97d87df4e004626a364eab867408\">leading a pivotal COVID-19 booster study at Baylor College of Medicine</a>, says while it \"wouldn't surprise me\" if J&#38;J recipients get a booster recommendation soon,&#160;\"for the Moderna, it is an open question.\"</p>\n\tThe protection Moderna's vaccine offers against hospitalization seems to last longer than other brands.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/614e2d78b414c10018625d8b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"chart showing vaccine effectiveness appears to wane more with pfizer than with moderna after 4 months\" height=\"1208\" width=\"2160\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/vaccines/acip/meetings/downloads/slides-2021-09-22/04-COVID-Link-Gelles-508.pdf\" target=\"_blank\">CDC ACIP meeting, September 22-23, 2021.</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>This data, collected from hospitals in 20 cities across the country, suggests that Moderna's vaccine protects people against hospitalization for longer than both Pfizer and Johnson &#38; Johnson.</p><p>After four months, Moderna's vaccine remained 92% effective at preventing hospitalizations, while Pfizer's was 77% effective, and J&#38;J's 68%.</p><p>&#160;</p>\n\tOne reason why Moderna may be holding up better in long-term protection is because the vaccine dosage is higher.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/614e2d79b414c10018625d91?format=jpeg\" alt=\"vaccine effectiveness chart showing slightly lower effectiveness against hospitalizations for pfizer vaccine than for moderna\" height=\"1196\" width=\"2104\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/vaccines/acip/meetings/downloads/slides-2021-09-22/04-COVID-Link-Gelles-508.pdf\" target=\"_blank\">CDC ACIP meeting, September 22-23, 2021.</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Moderna's <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-lower-dose-moderna-covid-19-vaccine-fewer-side-effects-2021-9\">shot consists of 100 micrograms</a> of mRNA vaccine, while Pfizer's is 30 micrograms. That may mean <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-19-vaccine-side-effects-moderna-pfizer-2021-2\">lighter side effects</a> for Pfizer's shot, but in the long run the protection might not be as strong.&#160;&#160;</p><p>According to a study of <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/mmwr/volumes/70/wr/mm7037e2.htm\">hospitals</a> in New York, Minnesota, Wisconsin, Utah, California, Oregon, Washington, Indiana, and Colorado, Moderna's vaccine is triggering far fewer hospitalizations when people aged 65 and older do get sick.&#160;</p>\n\tAnother possibility is that the four week interval between doses of Moderna is better than the three week waiting time between shots one and two of Pfizer.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/614e2d78b414c10018625d87?format=jpeg\" alt=\"vaccine effectiveness against hospitalization lower with pfizer than moderna\" height=\"1210\" width=\"1634\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/vaccines/acip/meetings/downloads/slides-2021-09-22/04-COVID-Link-Gelles-508.pdf\" target=\"_blank\">CDC ACIP meeting, September 22-23, 2021.</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Both vaccines are still great at preventing severe disease and hospitalization, especially in adults under the age of 65.</p><p>Still, this <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/norovirus/reporting/index.html\">data from five veterans affairs medical centers</a> in the US suggests that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-vaccine-protection-covid-hospitalization-compared-pfizer-cdc-study-2021-9\">Moderna's vaccine</a> is superior at protecting elderly adults, with a vaccine effectiveness of 87% against hospitalization in patients aged 65 and up, whereas Pfizer is 77% effective in that same group.&#160;</p>\n\tSince the Delta variant took over in the US, both Moderna and Pfizer recipients are getting sick more often. But Moderna's vaccine effectiveness against hospitalization, for people over age 30, is looking slightly stronger - for now.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/614e2d79b414c10018625d93?format=jpeg\" alt=\"charts showing vaccine effectiveness against hospitalization remains very high for both vaccines\" height=\"1124\" width=\"2146\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/vaccines/acip/meetings/downloads/slides-2021-09-22/04-COVID-Link-Gelles-508.pdf\" target=\"_blank\">CDC ACIP meeting, September 22-23, 2021.</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>These estimates of vaccine effectiveness, broken down by age group, come from data on over 74,000 hospitalizations across 187 hospitals nationwide.&#160;</p><p>Here, we can see that Moderna has been outperforming Pfizer among adults ages 30-64. From June to August, Moderna's vaccine effectiveness against hospitalization was 99% in the 30-49 year old age group and 91% among 50-64 year olds. Pfizer's vaccine during that same time period was roughly 82% effective among 30-49 year olds, and 84% effective among 50-64 year olds.</p><p>But in younger adults, ages 18-29, the two vaccines performed almost identically, with vaccine effectiveness against hospitalization of 82% for Moderna and 85% for Pfizer.</p><p>It's tough to know exactly how the arrival of the Delta variant in the spring may be impacting&#160; how well vaccines work.</p>\n\tWhichever way you slice the data, all the vaccines are still pretty stellar at their primary job - keeping people alive and out of the hospital. Still, older adults remain more vulnerable to severe COVID-19 outcomes, even when they're vaccinated.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/614e2d79b414c10018625d8e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"vaccine effectiveness chart showing protection remains high against hospitalization\" height=\"1202\" width=\"2156\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/vaccines/acip/meetings/downloads/slides-2021-09-22/04-COVID-Link-Gelles-508.pdf\" target=\"_blank\">CDC ACIP meeting, September 22-23, 2021.</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>This <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/covid-data/covid-net/purpose-methods.html\">data, taken from more than 250 hospitals</a> across 14 states, combines both the Pfizer and Moderna vaccine effectiveness against hospitalization in a single chart. It shows the vast majority of COVID-19 cases and deaths nationwide are now among unvaccinated people.&#160;</p><p>\"We will not boost our way out of this pandemic,\" CDC Director Rochelle Walensky said during a White House COVID-19 briefing on Friday. \"The most vulnerable are those unvaccinated.\"&#160;</p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a _740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=GJKbTliV1JQ:7See5Ddhz4Q:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn80@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-37-916_9cc632752f3e55b1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/GJKbTliV1JQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn79@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-33-167_b5f81a6a4348bd73.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761729131},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Concerns about <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd\">bitcoin</a>&#39;s <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/bitcoin-uses-more-energy-than-american-airlines-bank-of-america-2021-3\">heavy environmental impact</a> are pushing miners toward carbon-free nuclear energy as cities like Miami look to capitalize on the trend, according to a <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/bitcoin-miners-eye-nuclear-power-as-environmental-criticism-mounts-11632654002\">Wall Street Journal</a> report.</p><p>Miami Mayor Francis Suarez, who has fast become a <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/miami-crypto-bitcoin-biggest-hub-expatriate-experts-florida-2021-6\">beloved figure in crypto circles</a>, told the Journal that he has been pitching bitcoin mining firms on his city&#39;s nuclear facilities and crypto friendliness. </p><p>A Miami-based nuclear plant owned by Florida Power &#38; Light has been in talks with bitcoin miners over how to get ahold of cheap land near the facility to host mining rigs, Suarez told the Journal. He said worries about bitcoin&#39;s eco-unfriendliness &#34;come from the fact that a lot of the mining was being done in coal-producing countries.&#34;</p><p>In June, Suarez made a similar pitch to Chinese firms <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/china-bitcoin-crypto-crackdown-visuals-sichuan-mining-pool-2021-06\">displaced by Beijing&#39;s mining ban</a>.</p><p>&#34;The fact that we have nuclear power means that it&#39;s very inexpensive power,&#34; he told CNBC at the time. &#34;We understand how important this is … miners want to get to a certain kilowatt price per hour.&#34;</p><p>While bitcoin mining is a highly energy-intensive activity, using nuclear power generates nearly zero carbon emissions or air pollution - presenting a seemingly tidy fix to a growing concern.</p><p>Outside of Miami, too, miners are eyeing other opportunities to link with nuclear energy sources. </p><p>Nuclear startup Oklo Inc. for example, has signed a 20-year deal to supply energy to Compass Mining through its mini reactor. 2022","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/john-hinckley-jr-unconditional-release-reagan-attempted-assassin-2021-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6151d99cb414c1001862865c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"John Hinckley\" height=\"957\" width=\"1914\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>In this Nov. 18, 2003 file photo, John Hinckley Jr. arrives at U.S. District Court in Washington.\n<p class=\"copyright\">(AP Photo/Evan Vucci, File)</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>President Ronald Reagan&#39;s attempted Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>President Ronald Reagan&#39;s attempted assassin John Hinckley Jr. will be granted &#34;unconditional release&#34; in 2022.</p><p>&#34;&#39;I&#39;m going to after all these years grant unconditional release to Mr. Hinckley,&#34; Judge Paul L. Friedman said during a court hearing on Monday in the US District Court for the District of Columbia.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.secretservice.gov/reagan40thanniversary\">Hinckley Jr. shot Reagan, a police officer, a secret service agent, and Reagan&#39;s press secretary</a> in an attempt to win over child actress Jodie Foster in 1981. The court accepted Hinckley&#39;s insanity plea, leading the government to place Hinckley in a DC-based psychiatric facility, St. Elizabeth&#39;s Hospital.</p><p>&#34;He was ravaged by mental illness at the time,&#34; Hinckley&#39;s attorney, Barry William Levine, said in Monday&#39;s court hearing. &#34;It was that mental illness that was the basis of his acquittal.&#34;</p><p>Friedman said the court has granted Hinckley several additional freedoms in the past two decades, ultimately letting him live full-time with his mother in Williamsburg, Virginia, in 2016.</p><p>Hinckley&#39;s lawyer and US Attorney Kacie McCoy Weston both agreed with the judge&#39;s decision for a full and unconditional release. Both parties said they wanted to wait until June 2022 to release Hinckley to see how he responds to the recent death of his mother, which will result in him being by himself for the first time in decades.</p><p>&#34;The ball is completely in Mr. Hinckley&#39;s hands,&#34; Weston said.</p><p>In addition to lobbying from his attorneys, the Department of Behavioral Health at St. Elizabeth&#39;s Hospital wrote letters in 2020 and 2021 recommending Hinckley&#39;s unconditional release.</p><p>Friedman called Hinckley one of the most studied patients in the history of the institution, noting that very few people have been subjected to as many interviews, risk assessments, and testing as Hinckley.</p><p>&#34;If he hadn&#39;t tried to kill the president he would have been granted unconditional release a long, long time ago,&#34; Friedman said.</p><p>The judge finished Monday&#39;s hearing to say that after adjudicating Hinckley&#39;s case for many years, it&#39;s time for a change.</p><p>Hinckley &#34;should be able to live out his life productively in Williamsburg interacting with people doing his art, his music, and all will be right with the world,&#34; Friedman said. university described &#34;severe staffing shortages&#34; in its culinary-services team and said its residential dining halls would remain open only for people with MSU-issued ID cards.</p><p>It also said two cafeterias in residence halls and two Starbucks outlets on campus would reduce their opening hours.</p><p>The changes went into effect on Friday.</p><p>The university said some of the changes could remain throughout the fall semester. It added that it was &#34;competing for the same available talent&#34; as local businesses.</p><p>Many businesses across the US say they&#39;re struggling to find workers. While some businesses have said <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/origin-of-nobody-wants-to-work-anymore-2021-7\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"63abcc2a88f8ec6fd3a34d9a3d5ee34b\">people don&#39;t want to work anymore</a>, workers say they&#39;re quitting their jobs to seek <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/labor-shortage-hospitality-workers-restaurant-hotels-pay-wages-joblist-survey-2021-7\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"b7c8a77ffdf1a986092aceb12ce3623c\">better pay, more benefits, and improved working conditions</a>.</p><p>MSU described the decision as a difficult one but said it would reduce the impact of labor and food shortages.</p><p>The university <a href=\"https://www.wxyz.com/news/michigan-state-university-temporarily-closes-dining-halls-to-public-due-to-staffing-shortage\">told Detroit&#39;s ABC affiliate</a> on Friday that its culinary-services team needed about 470 full-time workers, 2,800 student workers, and 800 temporary and on-call employees to be fully operational. It did not say how many staff members it was short of.</p><p>The team dwindled when students returned home after in-person classes stopped in 2020, MSU said. Its student workers picked up jobs elsewhere and didn&#39;t come back, leaving gaps in the workforce, it added.</p><p>MSU didn&#39;t immediately respond to a request for comment from one line about housing along and a commitment to make its monetary policy flexible, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/world/china/china-evergrandes-electric-car-units-shares-tumble-23-after-warning-2021-09-27/\">Reuters</a> first reported Monday. The statement was made after the bank&#39;s third-quarter Monetary Policy Committee meeting.</p><p>Markets were rattled last week on fears that the fallout of a potential Evergrande default would reverberate across the globe. The beleaguered Chinese property developer missed a deadline to pay $83.5 million in interest on it dollar-denominated bond last week. Another <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/china-evergrande-debt-bonds-maturities-idUSL8N2QP1H5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$47.5 million coupon</a> is due this week on a second dollar bond. </p><p>As Evergrande teeters on the edge of insolvency, many investors have wondered if the Chinese government would step in to help prop it up. Some sources said China is letting Evergrande sweat to make its case that Chinese companies need to better manage their finances, the <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/09/26/business/china-evergrande-crisis.html?referringSource=articleShare\">New York Times</a> reported.</p><p>But on Monday, the PBOC said it commits to &#34;safeguard the legitimate rights of housing consumers.&#34; The Asian superpower, according to Teresa Kong, portfolio manager at Matthews Asia, has the financial tools to manage the situation if it takes a turn for the worse.</p><p>&#34;We believe Evergrande&#39;s financial problems are highly unlikely to create a risk to China&#39;s financial system,&#34; Kong said in a <a href=\"https://www.matthewsasia.com/insights/china/2021/evergrande-too-big-to-fail/\">note last week</a>. &#34;The company does have a large debt burden, but it is insignificant given the scale of China&#39;s financial system.&#34;</p><p>She pointed to two Chinese companies with similar debt burdens, Anbang and HNA, that were successfully restructured without spreading risk through the system.</p><p>&#34;As in the past, we expect the government to take an active role in managing the restructuring of Evergrande to mitigate the risks, by ensuring that its current liquidity problem does not become an insolvency problem and a bigger crisis of confidence in the Chinese financial system,&#34; she added.</p><p>Evergrande, with $309 billion in liabilities, is the world&#39;s most indebted company. data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"8a5ad3cb1f9a89a21b2839a560ae2afc\">7.3 billion square feet of contracted land</a>.</p><p> </p><p> </p><div business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Jeff Bezos&#39;s rocket firm, Blue Origin, is sending its next group of amateur astronauts to the edge of space in October. </p><p>The company&#39;s second human flight will take place on October 12 and, like last time, will transport four tourists around 62 miles skyward aboard the company&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jeff-bezos-risk-blue-origin-rocket-2021-6\">New Shepard rocket</a>. They&#39;ll experience a few minutes of weightlessness before floating back down to Earth in a pressurized capsule.</p><p>Blue Origin on Monday announced the <a href=\"https://www.blueorigin.com/news/next-human-flight-on-october-12\">identities of two customers who bought seats. </a></p><p>One is Chris Boshuizen, an Australian former NASA engineer and entrepreneur. During his stint at NASA&#39;s Ames Research Center from 2008 to 2012, Boshuizen served as a Space Mission Architect and helped invent the Phonesat, a satellite built out of a smartphone. </p><p>He went on to found and serve as CTO of Planet Labs, which uses nanosatellites to image the Earth&#39;s surface. Boshuizen is now a partner at venture capital firm DCVC. Planet Labs is a potential Blue Origin customer as it seeks to launch more of its &#34;dove&#34; satellites into orbit. </p><p>The other passenger is Glen de Vries, who founded the clinical research platform Medidata Solutions in 1999, which is now part of the French conglomerate Dassault Systèmes. </p><p>&#34;I&#39;ve spent my entire career working to extend people&#39;s lives. However, with limited materials and energy on Earth, extending our reach into space can help humanity continue to thrive,&#34; he said in a statement. </p><p>Blue Origin completed its <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jeff-bezos-launches-to-space-blue-origin-first-human-spaceflight-2021-7\">first human flight</a> in July with Bezos, his brother Mark Bezos, octogenarian aviator Wally Funk, and Oliver Daemen, the company&#39;s first paying customer, on board. The company says it has sold <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jeff-bezos-blue-origin-sold-100-million-space-tourism-tickets-2021-7\">$100 million</a> worth of tickets to space. </p><p>Blue Origin did not respond to questions about how much Boshuizen and de Vries paid for their seats. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Things Before the Opening Bell</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Major cryptocurrency exchanges are cutting ties with investors in mainland China after the country <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/china-crypto-bans-cryptocurrency-transactions-forbids-foreign-exchanges-service-citizens-2021-9\">declared all crypto-related transactions illegal</a>. </p><p>Friday&#39;s announcement also stops foreign crypto exchanges from providing services to local residents.</p><p>In response to the ban, Binance said it&#39;s no longer accepting registrations from Chinese mobile numbers. The exchange has been blocked in China since 2017, when the country ordered local crypto exchanges to cease operations, and local users have not been able to access its domain since then. </p><p>&#34;As such, Binance does not currently hold exchange operations in China,&#34; a Binance spokesperson told Insider. &#34;We can also confirm that Chinese mobile phone registrations are blocked and the Binance app is not available in China for downloading.&#34;</p><p>&#34;Binance takes its compliance obligations very seriously and is committed to following local regulator requirements wherever we operate,&#34; they added.</p><p>Chinese crypto exchange Huobi said on Sunday it would <a href=\"https://www.huobi.com/support/en-us/detail/54886961978434\">stop new user registrations</a> by mainland customers, and retire existing ones by the end of 2021. Huobi co-founder Du Jun <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/fintech-crypto-china/cryptocurrency-exchanges-rush-to-cut-ties-with-chinese-users-after-fresh-crackdown-idUSKBN2GN08A\">told Reuters</a> the exchange took corrective measures on the same day China clamped down on digital-asset transactions.</p><p>TokenPocket, a crypto wallet service provider that was widely used in China, <a href=\"https://www.theblockbeats.com/en/flash/49814\">said in a notice on Friday</a> it would &#34;actively embrace&#34; relevant regulatory provisions and end those services for mainland users that did not comply with the new laws.</p><p>China has been <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/china-crypto-crackdown-timeline-regulatory-bitcoin-ether-solana-dogecoin-bans-2021-9\">hostile towards cryptocurrencies</a> for a while now, so its latest announcement didn&#39;t shock many investors, or crypto businesses. That&#39;s evident from the recent <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/bitcoin-price-china-ban-cryptocurrency-transactions-crackdown-2021-9\">price action in the crypto market</a>, which didn&#39;t react as much in comparison to previous clampdowns. </p><p>Curtis Ting, managing director of Kraken&#39;s European operations, told Insider that China&#39;s ban won&#39;t have an impact on its business as most of its trading activity comes from clients based in the US, Europe, and other parts of the Asia Pacific.</p><p>Crypto exchanges might relocate to other more digital asset-friendly locations in the Asia Pacific or the Bahamas, Fundstrat strategist Armando Aguilar <a href=\"https://www.marketwatch.com/story/chinas-crypto-ban-has-almost-achieved-a-meme-like-status-but-here-are-the-lingering-impacts-11632512981?mod=home-page\">told MarketWatch</a>. Coinbase doesn&#39;t have any operations in China, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.coinbase.com%2Fplaces\">according to its website</a>.</p><p>FTX CEO Sam Bankman-Fried <a href=\"https://twitter.com/SBF_FTX/status/1441444101899972610\">announced Friday</a> the exchange had moved its headquarters <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/sam-bankman-fried-ftx-crypto-hong-kong-bahamas-relocates-headquarters-2021-9\">from Hong Kong to the Bahamas</a>, where it <a href=\"https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/ftx-establishes-substantial-presence-in-the-bahamas-and-appoints-ryan-salame-as-ceo-301380243.html\">established a subsidiary</a> only last week. </p><p>&#34;Countries that take such inflexible stances are taking significant, generational risks for their economies,&#34; John Wu, president of blockchain startup Ava Labs, said. &#34;They can find a way to embrace these networks, or be left out of the financial infrastructure of the future.&#34;</p><p><em><strong>Read More:</strong> <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/6151a4242fb46b0019be2e1b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Michael Burry big short\" height=\"1107\" width=\"2214\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Michael Burry.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jim Spellman/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Michael Burry said the recent surge in stocks reminded him of the dot-com bubble.</li>\n<li>&#34;The Big Short&#34; investor compared the options-trading boom to debt-fueled speculation in the 1920s.</li>\n<li>Burry has warned several times that a historic market crash is coming.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Michael Burry said the current market boom reminds him of the dot-com bubble, and compared the current options-trading frenzy to the rampant speculation that precipitated the Great Depression, in a flurry of recent tweets that have <a href=\"https://twitter.com/michaeljburry\">since been deleted</a>.</p><p>The Scion Asset Management chief tweeted a screenshot of Financialweb.com&#39;s stock chart. The defunct company behind Stock Detective and other financial-information websites saw its share price nosedive from a high of $28 to a fraction of a cent following the dot-com crash.</p><p>&#34;A very common chart back in the day,&#34; Burry said. &#34;Looks vaguely familiar.&#34;</p><p>Moreover, the hedge fund manager compared the bull market during the 15 years to 2000 to the run up in stocks over the past 15 years. He highlighted a 94% correlation between the Nasdaq 100&#39;s performance in each of those periods, and a 95% correlation for the S&#38;P 500 index.</p><p>The Scion chief also drew a parallel between the surge in people trading options on meme stocks such as AMC Entertainment, and the mass speculation that preceded the Wall Street Crash of 1929. He juxtaposed an article about the options mania with a quote by a statistician named Leroy Peavey in November 1929. Peavey blamed the market crash that year on a wave of leveraged speculation that pulled in &#34;elevator boys, typewriter girls, and even schoolchildren.&#34;</p><p>Burry is best known for predicting the collapse of the US housing bubble in the mid-2000s, and making a fortune by betting on a spike in subprime-mortgage defaults. His massive wager was chronicled in the book and the movie &#34;The Big Short.&#34;</p><p>The investor also bought a stake in GameStop and wrote several letters to the video-game retailer&#39;s board in 2019, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/big-short-investor-michael-burry-scion-gamestop-stock-price-frenzy-2021-2\">laying the groundwork</a> for the short squeeze on the stock this year and the broader meme-stock trend. He recently tweeted a picture of a subpoena he received from the Securities and Exchange Commission, ordering him to cooperate with the regulator&#39;s investigation into the GameStop saga. </p><p>Burry has been <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/big-short-michael-burry-tweets-tesla-robinhood-bitcoin-gamestop-bubble-2021-3\">sounding the alarm over Twitter</a> for several months. He&#39;s warned dangerous levels of speculation in meme stocks, cryptocurrencies, and other assets will lead to the &#34;<a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/big-short-michael-burry-warns-meme-stocks-crypto-crash-coming-2021-6\">mother of all crashes</a>.&#34; Scion was <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/big-short-michael-burry-tesla-stock-cathie-wood-ark-etf-2021-8?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">betting against</a> Elon Musk&#39;s Tesla and Cathie Wood&#39;s Ark Invest as of June 30.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/erik-gordon-market-dotcom-bubble-crash-cathie-wood-meme-stocks-2021-9?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">Veteran professor Erik Gordon outlines why he doesn&#39;t expect a stock-market crash, calls Cathie Wood a dot-com &#39;throwback&#39; for her grand claims, and warns against owning meme stocks</a></em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Greg Abbott over his state&#39;s restrictive law that prohibits abortions after six weeks of pregnancy with no exceptions for rape or incest.</p><p>After the ban took effect on September 1, the Republican governor faced immense criticism over its extreme measures and sought to defend the law by <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/abbott-says-he-will-eliminate-rape-texas-abortion-law-2021-9\">vowing to work</a> to &#34;eliminate rape&#34; and &#34;eliminate all rapists&#34; from the state.</p><p>Wallace pointed to Texas&#39; latest data on rape, citing that 15,000 cases were reported in 2019. &#34;Almost everyone says that that&#39;s a severe undercount,&#34; he told Abbott during an interview on his show &#34;Fox News Sunday.&#34;</p><p>&#34;Is it reasonable to say to somebody who is the victim of rape, and might not understand that they are pregnant until six weeks, &#39;Well don&#39;t worry about it because we&#39;re going to eliminate rape as a problem in the state of Texas?&#39;&#34; Wallace asked Abbott.</p><p>The Texas governor skirted around the question, saying that &#34;survivors of sexual assault deserve support, care and compassion&#34; and that the state plans to create a &#34;sexual assault survivors task force.&#34;</p><p>&#34;I got to point out about the ways that I have fought to arrest and apprehend and try to eliminate rape,&#34; Abbott added, before Wallace interjected.</p><p>&#34;Governor, excuse me, because we are running out of time,&#34; Wallace said. &#34;There were more than 15,000 rapes in 2019 when you were governor,&#34; he reiterated. </p><p>Wallace then pressed Abbott on whether he will amend the abortion law to include an exception for rape victims.</p><p>&#34;The goal is to protect the lives of every child with a heartbeat,&#34; Abbott responded.</p><p>&#34;Including the child of a rape?&#34; Wallace asked.</p><p>Abbott dismissed the question, claiming that the Republican-led state legislature would not push through a bill to revise the law.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-The Recount  (@therecount) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1442462325395623941?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">September 27, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p> </p><p>Beyond the lack of exception for cases of rape or incest, the Texas abortion law is considered the most restrictive in the country as it bans the procedure at a time before many people know they are pregnant. </p><p>The law has so far withstood legal challenges because of its unique enforcement mechanism. Rather than having state officials enforce the ban, the law invites ordinary citizens to do so. That means an individual can sue an abortion provider or anyone they believe who &#34;aids and abets&#34; someone getting the procedure beyond six weeks of pregnancy. Successful plaintiffs will be rewarded at least $10,000, in addition to legal fees.</p><p>The Supreme Court in a 5-4 vote on September 2 declined a request from abortion providers in Texas to block the law. The court&#39;s narrow majority argued that the decision was technical and the justices did not review the substance of the statute, which could still be legally challenged.</p><p>The nation&#39;s high court will consider a major abortion case, Dobbs v. Jackson Women&#39;s Health Organization, starting December 1. The case concerns a Mississippi law that bans nearly all abortions after 15 weeks of pregnancy, presenting a direct challenge to Roe v. Wade, the 1973 Supreme Court decision that guaranteed the right to an abortion until pre-viability, the point when a fetus can survive outside of the womb, which medical experts determine typically src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fda2a6b6524f10019792583?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The Crown\" height=\"2648\" width=\"3972\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>&#34;The Crown.&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Netflix</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Netflix dominated Nielsen&#39;s weekly streaming charts over the past year, a new analysis showed.</li>\n<li>&#34;The Crown&#34; had the most-viewed first week of any original streaming series, according to Nielsen.</li>\n<li>Nielsen&#39;s measurements - based on minutes watched - do give Netflix an edge, though.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/manifest-ruled-nielsens-streaming-charts-before-its-netflix-revival-2021-9\">new analysis</a> of Nielsen&#39;s weekly streaming charts over the past year shows that Netflix dominated.</p><p>Nielsen introduced weekly lists last year of the most-watched streaming titles, measured by the number of minutes watched per week. The <a href=\"https://www.evolutionmediacapital.com/research/1-year-nielsen-svod-top-10-lists\">analysis</a>, by Tavish Zausner-Mannes of the firm Evolution Media Capital, found the top 10 original streaming shows with the most-viewed weeks on Nielsen&#39;s lists from August 2, 2020 to August 8, 2021 - and they are all on Netflix.</p><p>The 10 shows with the most minutes watched in a given week included recent <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/netflix-ties-the-record-for-most-emmys-wins-with-44-2021-9\">Emmys champion</a> &#34;The Crown&#34; and &#34;Bridgerton,&#34; which is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bridgerton-compared-to-other-netflix-top-original-shows-viewership-2021-1\">Netflix&#39;s biggest worldwide series</a> of all time by its own calculations (<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-netflix-calculates-its-new-daily-top-10-lists-2020-2\">it counts a view</a> if an account watches at least two minutes of a show or movie). </p><p>The data accounted for each show&#39;s first full week on Netflix, which doesn&#39;t include premiere weekends, save for one: &#34;Cobra Kai&#34; had a big enough debut weekend that that week made the list with just three days of availability. </p><p>The data is limited in that Nielsen only measures US viewership and it includes just Netflix, Disney+, Hulu, and Prime Video. The way Nielsen measures viewership - total minutes watched - also gives Netflix shows an edge, as new seasons are released all at once while hits on other streaming services, such as Disney&#39;s &#34;The Mandalorian&#34; or Prime Video&#39;s &#34;The Boys,&#34; are released weekly.</p><p>Nielsen is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tv-tech-companies-that-could-replace-nielsen-2021-8\">also under fire this year</a> by the TV industry for the way it measures viewership, and NBCUniversal has taken steps <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nbcuniversal-is-taking-steps-to-replace-tv-measurement-firm-nielsen-2021-8\">to try and replace Nielsen</a> with other measurement companies. Still, the data illustrates which streaming shows were popular over the past year and reflects some underlying trends.</p><p><strong>Here are the top 10 streaming TV debuts of the past year, according to Nielsen measurements, including how many hours they were watched in their most-viewed week:</strong></p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\t10. \"Ratched\" (2020-present) - 27.2 million hours\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f4d04d77ffa48002894d1b7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"ratched netflix\" height=\"1340\" width=\"2066\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sarah Paulson in &#34;Ratched&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Netflix</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://www.netflix.com/title/80213445\"><strong>Description</strong></a>: \"In 1947, Mildred Ratched begins working as a nurse at a leading psychiatric hospital. But beneath her stylish exterior lurks a growing darkness.\"</p><p><strong>Rotten Tomatoes critic score</strong>: 61%</p><p><strong>What critics said</strong>: \"Sarah Paulson's sinister nurse bears almost no resemblance to the classic 1975 character.\" &#8212; <a href=\"https://www.nme.com/reviews/ratched-review-2756391\">NME</a> (season one)</p>\n\t9. \"The Haunting of Bly Manor\" (2020) - 30.4 million hours\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/614e1efa2fb46b0019be0a84?format=jpeg\" alt=\"haunting of bly manor - dani\" height=\"1973\" width=\"2631\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Victoria Pedretti as Dani Clayton.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Eike Schroter/Netflix</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><a href=\"https://www.netflix.com/title/81237854\">Description</a>:</strong> \"Dead doesn't mean gone. An au pair plunges into an abyss of chilling secrets in this gothic romance from the creator of 'The Haunting of Hill House.'\"</p><p><strong>Rotten Tomatoes critic score</strong>: 87%</p><p><strong>What critics said</strong>: \"'Bly Manor' stands as an ambitious blend of genres and arrives at its ultimate point with proper gravity. It's not a great ghost story, it's not a great love story, but it's still haunting enough to hear out.\" &#8212; <a href=\"https://www.indiewire.com/2020/10/the-haunting-of-bly-manor-review-netflix-1234591182/\">Indiewire&#160;</a></p>\n\t8. \"The Queen's Gambit\" (2020) - 30.8 million hours\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb67bc332f2170011f6ffc6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"queen&#39;s gambit\" height=\"1329\" width=\"1773\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Netflix</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong><a href=\"https://www.netflix.com/title/80234304\">Description</a>:</strong> \"In a 1950s orphanage, a young girl reveals an astonishing talent for chess and begins an unlikely journey to stardom while grappling with addiction.\"</p><p><strong>Rotten Tomatoes critic score</strong>: 96%</p><p><strong>What critics said</strong>: \"The series also succeeds in making the cerebral game of chess come alive even for viewers who don't know a rook from a pawn.\" &#8212; 00:55:28","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:28","title":"The CIA pitched Trump officials plans to assassinate Julian Assange while he was hiding in a London embassy in 2017, report says","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/cia-pitched-julian-assange-assassination-trump-officials-report-2021-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6151b21eb414c10018627d1f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"assange\" height=\"978\" width=\"1956\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Julian Assange, the founder of WikiLeaks, at the Embassy of Ecuador in London.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The CIA discussed &#34;options&#34; to assassinate or kidnap WikiLeaks&#39; founder in 2017, <a href=\"https://news.yahoo.com/kidnapping-assassination-and-a-london-shoot-out-inside-the-ci-as-secret-war-plans-against-wiki-leaks-090057786.html\">Yahoo News reported</a>.</li>\n<li>Director Mike Pompeo reportedly wanted revenge after WikiLeaks published secret CIA documents.</li>\n<li>Assange was at the time holed up in the Ecuadorian Embassy in London.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The CIA in 2017 pitched senior Trump administration officials plans to kidnap or assassinate the WikiLeaks founder Julian Assange, who was holed up in a London embassy, <a href=\"https://news.yahoo.com/kidnapping-assassination-and-a-london-shoot-out-inside-the-ci-as-secret-war-plans-against-wiki-leaks-090057786.html\">a Yahoo News investigation found</a>.</p><p>The report, which Yahoo News said was based on interviews with more than 30 former US officials, said the CIA was enraged by WikiLeaks&#39; publication in 2017 of thousands of documents detailing the agency&#39;s hacking and covert surveillance techniques, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cia-vault-7-leak-woefully-lax-security-protocol-report-2020-6?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">known as the Vault 7 leak</a>.</p><p>The Yahoo News report said senior officials inquired about &#34;options&#34; for what to do about Assange, including the feasibility of assassinating or kidnapping him.</p><p>CIA Director Mike Pompeo - who later became secretary of state - was determined to take revenge on Assange after the leak, Yahoo News reported.</p><p>In 2017, Pompeo <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cia-mike-pompeo-wikileaks-assange-2017-4\">designated WikiLeaks</a> a &#34;non-state hostile intelligence service,&#34; meaning it could be targeted with the same aggressive actions used against foreign states&#39; intelligence agencies.</p><p>A former senior counterintelligence official told Yahoo News that &#34;there seemed to be no boundaries&#34; during discussions with the Trump administration about Assange in 2017.</p><p>Pompeo and other senior officials &#34;were completely detached from reality because they were so embarrassed about Vault 7,&#34; a former national security official told the publication. &#34;They were seeing blood.&#34;</p><p>Yahoo News said it could not confirm whether the discussions were escalated to the Trump White House. The CIA and Pompeo did not immediately respond to Insider&#39;s request for comment.</p><p>In 2017, Assange was living in the Ecuadorian Embassy in London. He had been taking refuge there since 2012, after <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/julian-assange-sweden-rape-investigation-dropped-2019-11\">Swedish prosecutors opened an investigation</a> into him following allegations of rape and molestation.</p><p>Assange had claimed that if he were extradited to Sweden for questioning, he would be sent to the US, where he said he would face persecution. Assange had been charged in the US with offenses related to WikiLeaks&#39; publication <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/julian-assange-trump-administration-secret-charges-united-states-2019-1\">of thousands of confidential US diplomatic cables</a>.</p><p>Yahoo News reported that US officials picked up intelligence suggesting that Russia was planning to smuggle Assange out of the UK to Moscow, prompting a search for ways to ensure that he wouldn&#39;t escape.</p><p>Among the possible scenarios to prevent a getaway were engaging in a gun battle with Russian agents on the streets of London and ramming the car that Assange would be smuggled in, former officials told Yahoo News.</p><p>Ultimately, assassination plans were dropped because of legal concerns at the highest levels of the Trump administration, Yahoo News reported. The report also described concerns that a kidnapping would derail US attempts to prosecute Assange.</p><p>UK authorities arrested Assange in April 2019 after Ecuador withdrew its asylum protections. He is being held in the Belmarsh prison in London, as a UK judge in January refused the US&#39;s request for his extradition.</p><p>&#34;As an American citizen, I find it absolutely outrageous that our government would be contemplating kidnapping or assassinating somebody without any judicial process simply because he had published truthful information,&#34; Barry Pollack, Assange&#39;s lawyer in the US, told Yahoo News.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/bforoZEAY6w\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 27 Sep 2021 13:07:27 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/6151b23ab414c10018627d25?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"a6a04b3e239f400a0584efd705657624","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn59@2020_1/2021/09/27/16-55-38-949_113d68369d3c7923.webp","destWidth":1852,"destHeight":1389,"sourceBytes":82782,"destBytes":82782,"author":"tporter@businessinsider.com (Tom Porter)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/6151b21eb414c10018627d1f?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn11@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-32-704_281070a5b1daaece.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn72@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-37-727_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=bforoZEAY6w:S9hjTNZ39fw:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn72@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-36-505_24c3982e39657e13.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=bforoZEAY6w:S9hjTNZ39fw:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn71@2020_1/2021/09/27/16-55-38-216_33638a0cde65dfa8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn51@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-35-450_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=bforoZEAY6w:S9hjTNZ39fw:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn12@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-35-333_ed01d788e92c8fbd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/bforoZEAY6w":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn92@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-36-555_4f24c99e3071707c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761728375},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:28","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:28","title":"5 red flags that someone won't be a good leader at work","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/red-flags-work-leadership-promotion-narcissist-traits-2021-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e17796cb2e66a5f3c0a0423?format=jpeg\" alt=\"job interview\" height=\"4176\" width=\"5568\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Leaders should be approachable and not overbearing, or they&#39;ll risk limiting creativity and motivation.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Skynesher/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>If you want to keep good employees, you need to have strong managers. </li>\n<li>Not everyone is cut out for a leadership role, particularly people who show narcissistic tendencies. </li>\n<li>Leaders should be approachable, not overbearing, and eager to praise their direct reports&#39; success.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>As an executive coach, I do a lot of listening to managers worried about losing good employees. People-oriented managers understand what they need to do to <a href=\"https://www.inc.com/marcel-schwantes/5-ways-to-lead-with-emotional-courage-get-best-out-of-people.html\">get the best out of people</a>. I&#39;m not concerned about them.</p><p>I <em>am</em> concerned about managers being promoted into <a href=\"https://www.inc.com/marcel-schwantes/how-can-you-spot-really-good-leaders-they-do-any-of-these-5-things-exceptionally-well.html\">leadership roles</a> when they have no business being there. <a href=\"https://www.inc.com/marcel-schwantes/5-leadership-lessons-to-help-business-owners-thrive.html?cid=search\">Leadership</a> is demonstrated through competence, not attitude, confidence, or charisma. It takes ability and skills. </p><p>That&#39;s why the single biggest decision any organization will make is whom they name manager. When you name the wrong person manager, nothing fixes that bad decision.</p><p>We&#39;ve all heard this tune play like a broken record: <em>People leave managers, not companies.</em></p><p>So what have I seen over the course of 20 years that proves, beyond a shadow of a doubt, that someone is not fit to lead?</p><h2>1. Managers who look after only themselves</h2><p>These managers aren&#39;t concerned with fulfilling the company mission or aligning team goals to organizational objectives. It&#39;s about their individual performance and getting that annual bonus. Managers with this attitude are playing for the name on the back of the jersey and are concerned only about their own accomplishments and how they look to their superiors.</p><h2>2. Narcissistic tendencies</h2><p>This manager often belittles a team member&#39;s work and might even ridicule staff at meetings. When he needs something from you, he may become threatening. At his most toxic, he will make you doubt yourself and your ultimate value to the company.</p><h2>3. Treating people like numbers</h2><p>In top-down power structures, employees are considered to be objects or expenses rather than assets; there is little concern for their happiness or well-being since the motive for hiring them was purely productivity and profit. In these pressure-cookers, there&#39;s little evidence of leaders displaying compassion and empathy in seeing employees as valued human beings. As a result, you&#39;ll encounter high levels of stress, turnover, absenteeism, and burnout.</p><h2>4. Too much control</h2><p>The work environment is overbearing and stifling because managers want control over all decisions. Such managers distrust the team, so tasks rarely get delegated to others. There&#39;s hardly room for group discussion or input because the management style is autocratic, which limits creativity and the team&#39;s desire to learn new things. </p><h2>5. Taking the spotlight from the team</h2><p>The team puts together a wonderful product and the client is happy with the results. And then it happens: The manager takes all the credit. No praise for the team, no celebration of everyone&#39;s success, no recognition of team members for their contributions. This type of manager will steal the light and thunder away from the team, which is a total employee-engagement killer.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Things Before the Opening Bell</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Crypto exchange FTX has relocated its headquarters from Hong Kong to the Bahamas after planning the move for some time, its boss Sam Bankman-Fried said, rejecting the idea China&#39;s crypto ban played a part.</p><p>FTX had been considering the Bahamas for a while, as it is one of the first countries to roll out comprehensive regulation for cryptocurrencies, the company&#39;s founder and CEO <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=psr8rPysuLs\">told Bloomberg</a> in a Friday interview.</p><p>The crypto exchange has <a href=\"https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/ftx-establishes-substantial-presence-in-the-bahamas-and-appoints-ryan-salame-as-ceo-301380243.html\">registered a subsidiary</a> in the Bahamas, which <a href=\"https://www.institutionalassetmanager.co.uk/2020/12/16/293708/bahamas-dare-legislation-opens-door-new-industry\">brought in a legal framework</a> for services for trading digital tokens in December with the Digital Assets and Registered Exchanges Act.</p><p>Another factor is the Bahamas &#34;has emerged from COVID lively, safe, and without quarantine,&#34; Bankman-Fried flagged in a <a href=\"https://twitter.com/SBF_FTX/status/1441444101899972610\">tweet</a>.</p><p>News of the move came shortly after China declared all <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/china-crypto-bans-cryptocurrency-transactions-forbids-foreign-exchanges-service-citizens-2021-9\">crypto-related transactions illegal</a> and banned foreign exchanges from providing services to mainland residents. Crypto exchanges Binance and Huobi <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/china-crypto-ban-binance-huobi-cut-ties-mainland-users-reactions-2021-9\">scrambled to cut ties</a> with Chinese users after the ban.</p><p>But Bankman-Fried indicated FTX&#39;s decision to leave Hong Kong - seen as increasingly under the sway of Beijing - had nothing to do with that development.</p><p>&#34;This has been something which has been in the works for a while, and has been taking place for a while, and was not particularly in response to any very recent news,&#34; the 29-year-old crypto billionaire told Bloomberg.</p><p>China&#39;s edict caused somewhat of a slump in the crypto market Friday, but the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/bitcoin-price-china-ban-cryptocurrency-transactions-crackdown-2021-9\">price reaction was muted in comparison</a> with that following previous clampdowns. Bankman-Fried said that from a price point of view, China&#39;s move wouldn&#39;t have as much of an impact as some fear.</p><p> The FTX boss said he hopes there will be action by regulators around the world to ensure consumer protection and transparency, in a way that could support institutional involvement.</p><p>&#34;There is a risk that it takes a different direction, and that instead you see regulation coming out that effectively shuts down large swaths of the sector,&#34; he said.</p><p>&#34;I think that it would surprise me if that happened in a sort of coordinated way across the globe. But it&#39;s always a possibility.&#34;</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read More: </em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">&#39;You can bet small, win big&#39;: A top stock picker who returned an explosive 140% in the last year lays out the &#39;paranoid&#39; investing strategy that resulted in executive of YouTube defended the company&#39;s apparent acquiescence towards the Russian government, claiming free speech remains its &#34;core value.&#34; </p><p>Last week, Russian news service Interfax reported that Vladimir Putin&#39;s regime had <a href=\"https://www.interfax.ru/russia/785578\">ordered YouTube&#39;s parent company, Google, and Apple</a> to remove access to a voting app run by jailed opposition activist Alexey Navalny. The app <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-google-navalny-voting-app-russian-election-putin-opposition-2021-9\">disappeared from both app stores</a>, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/09/17/world/europe/russia-navalny-app-election.html\">sparking criticism</a> among both the public and <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-09-21/googlers-protest-removal-of-russian-app-as-bend-to-government\">Google&#39;s own employees</a>.</p><p>In an interview with <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-09-26/youtube-ceo-says-google-sees-free-speech-as-core-value-in-russia\">Bloomberg</a>, YouTube CEO Susan Wojcicki said free speech remained a &#34;core value&#34; at the company, but added that there were &#34;multiple considerations&#34; to take into account when dealing with a country like Russia. </p><p>The company <a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/technology-45471519\">has removed videos featuring Navalny</a> in the past, citing Russian censorship laws, and reportedly took down another of his group&#39;s campaign ads ahead of the country&#39;s parliamentary election.</p><p>Wojcicki did not give a direct answer when asked if the latest video had been removed at the Russian government&#39;s request. </p><p>&#34;One of the things that is important to us at YouTube is the fact that we do enable so many voices, and that we do enable people to express themselves, and really celebrate the freedom of speech,&#34; she said. &#34;That&#39;s a core value of ours.&#34; </p><p>&#34;But when we work with governments, there are many things that we have to take in consideration, whether it&#39;s local laws or what&#39;s happening on the ground,&#34; she added. &#34;So there&#39;s always going to be multiple considerations.&#34;</p><p>When pressed on who ordered the takedowns, Wojcicki said: &#34;We certainly get requests from governments, and we look and consider why are we getting the request? What&#39;s actually happening on the ground? And based on a whole bunch of different factors, we make a decision.&#34; </p><p>Navalny is currently in a Russian prison after returning to the country from Germany, where he recovered from being poisoned with the nerve agent Novichok during an internal Russian flight last August. The Russian government claims he is guilty of embezzlement.</p><p>On Friday, Navalny tweeted that he was surprised &#34;how obediently the almighty Big Tech&#34; had acted as Putin&#39;s &#34;accomplices&#34; in censoring him.</p><p>&#34;The giants Apple and Google have complied with the Kremlin&#39;s demands and removed our app from their stores. scores","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tesla-software-update-how-is-safety-score-calculated-2021-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6011ef0e6dfbe10018e00622?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tesla Model S interior\" height=\"863\" width=\"1725\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla Model S interior.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tesla</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Elon Musk <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-full-self-driving-elon-musk-beta-update-safety-score-2021-9\">announced a highly anticipated software update</a> on Saturday, despite criticism from regulators.</li>\n<li>The update allows drivers with favorable daily safety scores to request its Full Self-Driving beta.</li>\n<li>See the five safety factors and the final formula used by Tesla to calculate each score. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Elon Musk announced a <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1441560961593262081\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"7305e851c1cddc2306285af806ea7495\">highly anticipated software update</a> for Tesla vehicles on Saturday that allows drivers to view daily &#34;safety scores.&#34;</p><p>If drivers earn a favorable safety score for one week, they can then request access to Tesla&#39;s Full Self-Driving (FSD) beta software. </p><p>The score, ranging from zero to 100, assesses driving behavior based on five safety factors: forward-collision warnings per 1,000 miles, hard braking, aggressive turning, unsafe following, and forced autopilot disengagement. </p><p>As detailed in a <a href=\"https://www.tesla.com/support/safety-score#top\">safety guide published by Tesla</a>, the daily score is calculated through a Predicted Collision Frequency (PCF) formula. The final calculation is an estimate of how many collisions may occur per 1 million miles of driving. </p><p>Tesla drivers who earn a &#34;safe&#34; driving record for an entire week can then access the FSD Beta software, Insider&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-full-self-driving-elon-musk-beta-update-safety-score-2021-9\">Shalini Nagarajan reported</a> Sunday. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6151e606b414c10018628ae1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tesla&#39;s Safety Score Beta\" height=\"911\" width=\"1823\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla&#39;s Safety Score Beta\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.tesla.com/support/safety-score#five-factors\" target=\"_blank\">Tesla</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Some Tesla drivers have documented their experience with the new scoring system on social media. One user posted incremental changes in his score, claiming that &#34;running yellow lights&#34; and &#34;rolling through stop signs&#34; helped increase his rating, though Insider has not confirmed these claims.</p><p>Later, the user posted a screenshot of an almost-perfect score of 99, with the caption &#34;After driving like grandma all weekend.&#34;</p><p>On Reddit, users said hard acceleration such as &#34;gunning it at green lights&#34; did not appear to affect their safety score. </p><p>&#34;Have gunned it at all green lights. Can confirm safety score is still 92,&#34; one user wrote on the <a href=\"https://www.reddit.com/r/teslainvestorsclub/comments/pv2kbs/tesla_safety_score_beta/?utm_source=share&utm_medium=web2x&context=3ontext=3\">Tesla Investors Club</a> Reddit page. </p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Gary Black  (@garyblack00) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1441986455979511808?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">September 26, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p> </p><p>Tesla said it expects the formula to change in the future as it gains more customer and data insights. 00:55:28","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:28","title":"China's ban on crypto has sent traders piling into decentralized exchanges. Here's a look at what DEX is and what tokens to watch","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/china-crypto-ban-uniswap-sushiswap-dxdy-decentralized-exchanges-tokens-ether-2021-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6151e9c02fb46b0019be3e79?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Uniswap\" height=\"1096\" width=\"2193\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Uniswap\n<p class=\"copyright\">Barks/ Shutter Stock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>China&#39;s crypto ban last week has sent traders flocking to decentralized exchanges.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\">These peer-to-peer platforms allow parties to trade without any intermediary, even a clearing house.</li>\n<li>We take a look at how these exchanges work and which coins are the &#34;DEX&#34; big guns.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\"><strong>Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>The crypto market bounced back on Monday from the slump caused late last week by China&#39;s outright ban on trading and mining. But it&#39;s not been the major cryptocurrencies that have seen most of the action, or even some of the recent red-hot &#34;altcoins&#34;, but rather, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/crypto-uniswap-sushi-china-selloff-decentralized-exchange-tokens-ether-2021-9\">decentralized exchange (DEX) tokens</a>. </p><p>Decentralized exchanges don&#39;t rely on any intermediaries, as a standard centralized exchange would. There are no banks or brokers, or even <a href=\"https://www.investopedia.com/terms/c/clearinghouse.asp\">clearing houses</a> involved, but rather, they offer a peer-to-peer platform where the parties involved use smart contracts to execute their trades. </p><p>These contracts are mini-programs that run on a blockchain that will automatically execute once a set of conditions are met. A number of decentralized exchanges are built on the ethereum network - the largest such blockchain that hosts smart contacts, decentralized finance applications and other protocols. </p><p>They are often cheaper to use than centralized exchanges, like Binance or Coinbase, and mean users are completely in charge of managing their wallets and private keys, which allow them access to their crypto tokens. </p><p>The three biggest decentralized exchanges by volume are Uniswap, SushiSwap and derivatives exchange DxDy. </p><p>&#34;Decentralized exchanges Uniswap and Sushiswap have seen a surge in usage, which is likely a result of China&#39;s ban on centralised exchanges. Since DEX&#39;s only require a crypto wallet and no KYC [know your customer], it is much easier to use and can be set up in a matter of minutes,&#34; Jonas Luethy, junior sales trader at digital asset manager Global Block, said in a newsletter. </p><p>There are basically three different ways a DEX will function.</p><p>The first is with what&#39;s known as an on-chain order book that lists all buy and sell orders sorted by price. In this case, every part of the transaction is written onto the blockchain. That includes not just purchases and sales, but even requests to buy or sell. So all the information is stored safely in one place, but this process can be costly and slower.</p><p>Off-chain order books only record the final settled transaction on the blockchain, without storing orders or any other information. It&#39;s faster, but a little less secure than on-chain.</p><p>Lastly, there are automated market makers (AMM) that use what are known as liquidity pools. The pool is essentially made up of a big enough reserve of tokens, or pairs of tokens. </p><p>A user will just place the tokens they wish to sell or buy in the pool and one smart contract will complete their transaction. This method makes it much easier to swap from one cryptocurrency to another than with an order book, for example.</p><p>Here are the top 3 DEX tokens to watch out for: </p><ol><li aria-level=\"1\">Uniswap is the biggest token, with a market capitalization of over $14 billion. The token surged by almost 40% at one point on Monday. It&#39;s up around 360% so far this year at around $23.40. </li><li aria-level=\"1\">Sushi is the second biggest token, with a market cap of over $1 billion. Its token, which has risen around 270% this year to $10.70, rallied by nearly 30% earlier on Monday.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">DYDX gained by as much as 31% Monday. The underlying exchange has seen a massive influx of new users plus, and for the first time, has registered higher trading volumes than Coinbase, according to GlobalBlock. The dydx token launched around a month ago and has already roughly doubled in value to around $20.00. </li></ol><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/6151e9cd2fb46b0019be3e7f?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"d05e9be2f20c7220f62555871e4ebaea","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn71@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-39-214_fe2ed2d9368ddcec.webp","destWidth":2193,"destHeight":1644,"sourceBytes":42082,"destBytes":42082,"author":"cshumba@insider.com (Camomile Shumba)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/6151e9c02fb46b0019be3e79?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn39@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-33-794_4d94e9ccd38a2d59.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn72@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-37-727_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zbDL7j3ZaGc:0HTjpPRiCps:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn8@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-34-085_160ad16ede8804ec.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zbDL7j3ZaGc:0HTjpPRiCps:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn18@2020_2/2021/09/27/16-55-32-696_341c48926d149fcc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn51@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-35-450_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zbDL7j3ZaGc:0HTjpPRiCps:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn15@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-38-817_be70569d760a0972.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/zbDL7j3ZaGc":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn19@2020_2/2021/09/27/16-55-36-342_d7c31f59673d82c3.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761728344},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:28","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:28","title":"Why the US government could shut down this week and what will happen","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/will-government-shut-down-what-will-happen-debt-ceiling-congress-2021-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/525781f369beddb3126c3097?format=jpeg\" alt=\"government shutdown\" height=\"2525\" width=\"3366\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The US government is funded through September 30, and lawmakers are at an impasse to vote on a solution.</li>\n<li>If they don&#39;t vote to keep it funded, the government could shut down, causing furloughs and economic chaos.</li>\n<li data-stringify-indent=\"0\" data-stringify-border=\"0\">Senate Republicans <strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\">say they</strong> plan to torpedo a measure that would<strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"> &#34;pause&#34; </strong>the debt ceiling<strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"> debate for two months</strong>.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>It&#39;s shaping up to be a wild week in the halls of Congress, as a new infrastructure package is on the line and a potential government shutdown looms.</p><p>Thursday, September 30, is the end of the fiscal year - and the last day for which the federal government has funding. That means that lawmakers need to step in and pass what&#39;s called a &#34;continuing resolution&#34; measure that would temporarily fund the government. If they can&#39;t pass that, the government risks a possible shutdown, which could cause government employee furloughs and a ripple effect throughout the entire economy.</p><p>The House has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/house-approves-bill-government-shutdown-default-gop-set-to-oppose-2021-9\">passed</a> the continuing resolution that would fund the government for two more months. Crucially, that resolution also contains a measure that would suspend the debt ceiling through December 2022 - delaying this decision until after the midterm election.</p><p>Indeed, Minority Leader Mitch McConnell has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/house-approves-bill-government-shutdown-default-gop-set-to-oppose-2021-9\">made it clear</a> that the House bill with the debt ceiling suspension will not make it past the Senate. Instead, Republicans are arguing that the measure should pass through the party-line reconciliation Democrats are gearing up for. Though Republicans have not made any demands in exchange for an approval of the debt ceiling suspension, they&#39;ve instead made the suspension an issue of partisanship.</p><p>According to the <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/us-policy/2021/09/20/white-house-debt-ceiling/\">Washington Post</a>, McConnell told Punchbowl News that &#34;Democratic leaders have every tool and procedure they need to handle the debt limit on a partisan basis, just like they are choosing to handle everything else.&#34; But Democrats <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mitch-mcconnell-democrats-debt-ceiling-russian-roulette-with-the-economy-2021-9\">have said</a> that there&#39;s not enough time to address it in reconciliation.</p><p>&#34;The debt ceiling will be raised as it always should be, but it will be raised by the Democrats,&#34; McConnell said in a press conference on September 21. </p><p>During a government shutdown, many non-essential government services are paused, affecting everything from your mortgage approval to your visit to a national park. That&#39;s because some government employees are furloughed when agencies temporarily close; in 2019, amidst the most recent shutdown, Insider&#39;s Bob Bryan <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/government-shutdown-federal-workers-get-zero-dollar-paycheck-furlough-backpay-2019-1\">reported</a> that 800,000 federal employees received paychecks for $0. </p><p>At the time, the workers not receiving paychecks owed over $400 million in rent and mortgage payments, according to <a href=\"https://www.zillow.com/research/shutdown-mortgage-rent-22615/\">real-estate firm Zillow</a>. Some of those impacted workers turned to GoFundMe campaigns for help paying off their bills, Insider&#39;s Mariana Alfaro <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/government-shutdown-gofundme-pages-2019-1\">reported</a>. </p><h2>30 years of government shutdowns</h2><p>Treasury Secretary Janet Yellen <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nancy-pelosi-raise-the-debt-ceiling-janet-yellen-default-2021-9\">warned</a> Congress earlier this month that the country&#39;s ability to pay its bills will likely run out sooner than planned. After Congress missed a July 30 deadline to raise or suspend the debt ceiling, the US Treasury employed &#34;extraordinary measures&#34; to allow the government to continue paying its bills, but Yellen said those measures will likely run out in October due to financial uncertainty caused by the pandemic.</p><p>As Insider&#39;s Ben Winck and Joseph Zeballos-Roig previously <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-debt-ceiling-explained-democrats-republicans-government-spending-borrowing-2021-9\">reported</a>, the debt ceiling was introduced in 1917 and has since been raised 57 times to prevent the government from defaulting. And while the US has always managed to avoid a default to prevent a lapse in critical benefits and an economic recession, raising the limit has become more of a bargaining chip than a true financial threshold. </p><p>The first debt ceiling-related government shutdown took place in 1995, when then-Speaker of the House Newt Gingrich <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2021/09/22/republicans-usually-lose-shutdown-fights-so-why-are-they-going-there-again/?utm_source=feedly&utm_medium=referral&utm_campaign=wp_politicspolitics\">demanded</a> President Bill Clinton implement the Republicans&#39; proposal for a balanced budget, and ultimately caused the government to shut down for 21 days. </p><p>And similar political battles continued in following years. For example, in 2013 under President Barack Obama, the GOP refused to raise the debt ceiling unless the Affordable Care Act was defunded, causing the government to shut down for 16 days. </p><p>Most recently, President Donald Trump oversaw the longest government shutdown - 35 days - when Democrats refused to vote for increased funding for Trump&#39;s border wall between the US and Mexico. Notably, during all of these shutdowns, the government still did not go into default on its debt.</p><p>Speaker of the House Nancy Pelosi plans to address raising the debt ceiling, the infrastructure bill, and Democrats&#39; social spending bill this week, but it is unclear what path she will take if Democrats fail to garner enough votes to keep the government funded.</p><div src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fb1d670729770012b9b073?format=jpeg\" alt=\"coronavirus hospital texas\" height=\"2002\" width=\"4005\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Dr. Joseph Varon (right) speaks to a id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>COVID-19 is continuing to devastate predominately Republican states and regions largely due to stubborn vaccine refusal and hesitancy in red regions of the country. </p><p>A series <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/09/27/briefing/covid-red-states-vaccinations.html?smid=tw-share\">of new charts and graphics from The New York Times</a> demonstrate the increasingly stark partisan divides in vaccination and how they drive outbreaks in areas that voted for former President Donald Trump in 2020. </p><p>Nationwide, 75% of eligible Americans aged 12 and up have received at least one vaccine dose with 65% considered fully vaccinated, according to data<a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2020/us/covid-19-vaccine-doses.html\"> from the Centers for Disease Control. </a></p><p>But the data broken down at the state and county level show that Democratic areas account for far more of the country&#39;s vaccinations. </p><p>Nineteen out of the top 20 states and the District of Columbia with the highest vaccination rates among adults aged 18+ voted for President Joe Biden in 2020, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2020/us/covid-19-vaccine-doses.html\">according to The Times&#39; data,</a> while 19 of the 2020 states with lowest vaccination rates among that age group voted for Trump. </p><p>According to mid-September data <a href=\"https://www.kff.org/policy-watch/the-red-blue-divide-in-covid-19-vaccination-rates/\">from the Kaiser Family Foundation</a>, 52.8% of people in counties that voted for Biden are fully vaccinated compared to 39.9% in counties that voted for Trump, a nearly 13 percentage point gap. </p><p>The Times&#39; charts and visuals show a strong positive correlation between a state&#39;s 2020 vote share for Trump and COVID-19 cases and deaths, but a strong negative correlation between 2020 Trump share and vaccination rates. </p><p>While cases have begun to decline nationwide, states and regions that voted for Trump are continuing to get hit the hardest by the Delta variant, which ravaged states like Missouri, Arkansas, Florida, and other southern states over the summer. </p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2021/us/covid-cases.html?name=styln-coronavirus&region=TOP_BANNER&block=storyline_menu_recirc&action=click&pgtype=Interactive&variant=1_Show&is_new=false=1_Show&#38;is_new=false\">states with the current worst per-capita rates of COVID-19</a> are Alaska, Wyoming, West Virginia, Montana, and Kentucky, and all states in the top 10 highest per-capita COVID-19 rates voted for Trump in 2020. </p><p>The disparities in vaccine rates have also led to a sharp divergence in death rates at the county level. According to data analyzed by healthcare expert Charles Gaba cited by The Times, COVID-19 has killed 47 out of every 100,000 people in counties Trump won by over 70% but only 10 out of 100,000 people in counties where Trump received about a third of the vote share. </p><p>With efforts at persuading the unvaccinated continuing to hit a wall, some localities, colleges and universities, and employers are now mandating vaccination or weekly testing as a condition of employment or entering indoor venues.</p><p>But vaccine requirements have been flashpoints in political tugs-of-war between Republican governors like Gov. Ron DeSantis of Florida and Gov. Greg Abbott, who have moved to ban such mandates, and localities and private businesses who have sought to impose them. </p><p>The Biden administration is taking a more aggressive stane countering vaccine refusal, with Biden recently introduicing new mandates including a federal requirement for employers with 100 or more workers to establish a vaccination or weekly testing mandate for employees.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-19-vaccine-refusal-continues-to-wallop-impact-republican-states-2021-9'>Business
