00:55:28","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:28","title":"Binance bans users in Singapore from trading crypto as the country tightens its clampdown on the exchange","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/binance-singapore-bans-trading-crypto-october-exchange-fiat-swap-mas-2021-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6102c139aedf2100190eea08?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Binance\" height=\"1771\" width=\"3542\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Binance.\n<p class=\"copyright\">akub Porzycki/NurPhoto via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Binance said users in Singapore will no longer be permitted to buy and sell crypto from its main platform beginning October 26.</li>\n<li>This includes fiat deposit services, spot trading of crypto, purchase of crypto through fiat channels, and liquid swap.</li>\n<li>The move comes after Singapore&#39;s central bank on September 2 said Binance could be breaching local laws.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\"><strong>Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Binance announced Monday that users of its main platform in Singapore will no longer be permitted to buy and sell cryptocurrencies beginning October 26, amid the country&#39;s tightening clampdown on digital asset platforms.</p><p>The announcement comes as the cryptocurrency exchange also said it&#39;s <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/china-crypto-ban-binance-huobi-cut-ties-mainland-users-reactions-2021-9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">no longer accepting registrations from Chinese mobile numbers</a> after Beijing banned crypto transactions.</p><p>In Singapore, <a href=\"http://binance.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">binance.com</a> users <a href=\"https://www.binance.com/en/support/announcement/34c6c158d03a4877a4e13cf0927468bc\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">will not be allowed</a> to access certain functions such as fiat deposit services, spot trading of cryptocurrencies, the purchase of cryptocurrencies through fiat channels, and liquid swap.</p><p>Users, Binance said, are encouraged to &#34;cease all related trades, withdraw fiat assets and redeem tokens ... to avoid potential trading disputes.&#34;</p><p><a href=\"http://binance.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">Binance.com</a> is separate from Binance Asia Services, a separate entity that operates Binance Singapore (<a href=\"http://binance.sg/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">binance.sg</a>). BAS has submitted a license application to Singapore&#39;s central bank.</p><p>The move followed a <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/binance-crypto-trading-singapore-dollars-crackdown-monetary-authority-bans-warnings-2021-9\">September 6</a> restriction when Binance said it will not offer products in Singapore dollars and will stop all online communication operations in the country. Binance also said it will remove its app from the country&#39;s Apple and Google pay stores and stop all online communication, including its Telegram channel. </p><p>The successive announcements came after Singapore&#39;s central bank, the Monetary Authority of Singapore, on September 2 said Binance could be breaching local laws.</p><p>MAS then put Binance.com on its <a href=\"https://www.mas.gov.sg/investor-alert-list\">investor alert list</a>, which alerts residents to any unregulated platforms that have &#34; been wrongly perceived as being licensed or regulated&#34; by the central bank.</p><p>Binance has been under intense scrutiny from global regulators over numerous concerns, such as cryptocurrencies being used in money laundering. Its decentralized operations, having no formal headquarters since its founding in 2017, have also had authorities from various countries scratching their heads.</p><p>But in September, Binance finally admitted it needed a <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/binance-changpeng-zhao-cryptocurrency-regulators-warnings-bans-headquarters-2021-9?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">centralized headquarters</a> to work well with regulators all over the world, after being <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/binance-uk-fca-risk-financial-regulation-crypt-exchange-changpeng-zhao-2021-8?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">slapped with multiple warnings</a>, and in some jurisdictions, banned from operating due to its failure to register with local regulators.</p><p>Most recently, Binance on <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/binance-crypto-derivatives-futures-australia-regulator-options-leveraged-stop-close-2021-9\">September 23</a>, said it is shutting down cryptocurrency derivative products for existing customers in Australia by the end of the year to appease regulators.</p><p>Singapore has joined the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/britain-bans-cryptocurrency-exchange-binance-from-operating-in-uk-2021-6?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestmp;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">UK,</a> <a href=\"https://www.theblockcrypto.com/linked/109736/binance-blocks-ontario-canada-users?utm_source=feedly&utm_medium=rss=rss=rss=rss=rss=rss=rss\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Canada</a>, <a href=\"https://www.theblockcrypto.com/linked/109623/japan-fsa-another-warning-binance-unregistered-operations\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Japan</a>, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/technology/germanys-financial-watchdog-warns-crypto-exchange-binance-over-stock-tokens-2021-04-29/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Germany</a>, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/currencies/binance-thailand-sec-criminal-complaint-cryptocurrency-exchange-license-approve-2021-7?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingesttm_medium=ingest\" REUTERS/Keith Bedford/File Photo\" height=\"1750\" width=\"3500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Boston Fed President Eric Rosengren.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Boston Fed President Eric Rosengren said he would step down effective Thursday to focus on his health.</li>\n<li>He and another Fed president had bought stock in big-name firms, including Apple, Alibaba, and Tesla.</li>\n<li>Last week, Fed Chair Jerome Powell announced a fresh review of the ethics rules surrounding stock trades.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Boston Fed President Eric Rosengren said on Monday that he is resigning several months early due to health issues, following recent controversy over his stock purchases.</p><p>In a letter to Fed Chair Jerome Powell, Rosengren said he would step down effective Thursday to focus on his health.</p><p>&#34;While working on the pandemic relief programs for money market mutual funds and small businesses, given the long hours and stress, regrettably my kidney function declined significantly to the point that I qualified for the kidney transplant list,&#34; he wrote.</p><p>Rosengren, who is 64, said that preparations had been underway for his retirement next year, as Fed presidents are age-limited at 65 <a href=\"https://www.newyorkfed.org/medialibrary/media/aboutthefed/presidential-search/faqs.pdf\">in most cases</a>.</p><p>The letter did not mention the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/fed-presidents-kaplan-rosengren-share-trades-conflicts-interest-apple-tesla-2021-09\">stock-trading scandal that has roiled the Fed in recent weeks</a>, sparked by disclosures that Rosengren and Dallas Fed President Robert Kaplan had purchased stock in several big-name firms including <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/aapl-stock\">Apple</a>, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/baba-stock\">Alibaba</a>, and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/tsla-stock\">Tesla</a>. That prompted <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.wsj.com%2Farticles%2Ffed-faces-calls-to-remove-officials-over-trades-they-made-while-setting-policy-11632226559%3Fmod%3Darticle_inline\">calls by activists and former Fed officials</a> for Rosengren and Kaplan to step down or be fired.</p><p>In particular, Rosengren also made active trades in real estate investment trusts, raising eyebrows about past comments he has made about risks to real estate markets. </p><p>At a Fed meeting last week, Powell said that &#34;no one [at the Fed] is happy&#34; about the situation and announced a fresh review of the ethics rules surrounding stock trades.</p><p>&#34;We understand very well that the trust of the American people is essential for us to effectively carry out our mission, and that&#39;s why I directed the Fed to begin a comprehensive review of the ethics rules around permissible financial holdings and activity by Fed officials,&#34; said Powell.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read Ernst/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The SEC is cracking down on trading in 2,000 penny stocks, including Sears and Blockbuster, according to Reuters.</li>\n<li>Online brokers like Schwab and Fidelity have already stopped new share purchases ahead of the SEC rule.</li>\n<li>Retail investors have piled into penny or microcap stocks in the last year, egged on by the rise of online brokerages.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\">.</strong></a></li>\n</ul><p>The Securities and Exchange Commission is rolling out a new rule cracking down on trading in penny stocks, including Sears and Blockbuster, according to a <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/usa-sec-pink-sheets/u-s-pink-sheets-in-shakeup-as-securities-regulator-looks-to-stamp-out-fraud-idUSKBN2GJ0TS\">Reuters</a> report.</p><p>The rule requires certain stocks that trade over the counter to disclose more information, such as recent financial data. That could potentially force 1,000 to 2,000 stocks to delist for some time.</p><p>Online brokers including Schwab and Fidelity have already stopped new share purchases ahead of the SEC rule, according to Reuters. Shareholders will still be able to sell, but brokers are warning that liquidity will dry up.</p><p>Affected stocks include the shell companies liquidating bankrupt <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/shldq-stock\">Sears</a> and Blockbuster. These once-hyped firms trade alongside the likes of <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/lkncy-stock\">Luckin Coffee</a>, the upstart Chinese cafe chain that fell to accounting fraud. </p><p>Retail investors have piled into over-the-counter stocks, also called penny or microcap stocks, egged on by the rise of online broker platforms. Penny stock trading volume peaked at 1.9 trillion transactions in February. And even in August, volume remained more than double last year&#39;s levels, according to FINRA data cited by Reuters.</p><p>The SEC argues it is ending a loophole that allowed some penny-stock companies to mislead investors by withholding key information. But Daniel Zinn, a lawyer for OTC Markets Group, which hosts the affected penny stocks, said the opposite may end up being true.</p><p>&#34;We&#39;re in agreement with the SEC&#39;s goals of providing as much disclosure as possible,&#34; said Zinn. But he added that some tiny companies might not be able to pay for the cost of providing paperwork, and others may be wary of promoting trading in their stock. </p><p>&#34;In those circumstances, no quotes at all may lead to more harm than help for existing investors,&#34; said Zinn.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
